{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01Gxp5bsP9scxMkN7f8r6Jbe","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"OK, so now I understand the code flow better. In `azx_rirb_get_response`:\n\n1. Line 875: If `polling_mode` is set OR `do_poll` is set, it manually updates the RIRB\n2. Line 898-904: If NOT in polling mode and poll_count < 2, try polling once more\n3. Line 908-913: If NOT in polling mode, switch to polling mode\n4. Line 916-928: If MSI is enabled, disable it and try again\n5. Line 948-951: If still failing, switch to single_cmd mode\n\nSo the issue is:\n- Once `polling_mode` is set to 1, it stays 1 forever (it's never reset to 0)\n- When resuming from suspend, the hardware might have been properly reset, but the driver is still in polling_mode because the flag was never reset\n\nLooking back at the suspend code:\n```c\nstatic int azx_suspend(struct device *dev){\n    ...\n    azx_stop_chip(chip);  // Sets chip->initialized = 0, but does NOT reset polling_mode\n    ...\n}\n```\n\nSo the bug is: When resuming, we need to reset the polling_mode flag back to 0, just like we reset the chip->initialized flag.\n\nBut wait, let me also check when polling_mode might be used. Maybe it's not used at all after resume? Let me think about this more:\n\nWhen azx_init_chip is called with full_reset=1:\n- It resets the controller\n- It clears and enables interrupts\n- It initializes the codec command I/O\n- It sets chip->initialized = 1\n\nBut it does NOT reset polling_mode. So if polling_mode was set to 1 before suspend, it will still be 1 after resume.\n\nThen, when the driver tries to communicate with the codec after resume, if there's any timeout (even a temporary one), it will enter the polling mode path. But the problem is more subtle:\n\n\nThe polling_mode flag persists across suspend/resume cycles, so every codec communication after resume will manually poll for responses instead of relying on interrupts. This creates a race condition where both the interrupt handler and the polling code might be accessing the RIRB simultaneously, causing synchronization issues. The symptom of \"choppy sound with 2-second silences\" suggests the audio pipeline is getting stuck waiting for codec responses that aren't being properly synchronized.\n\nLooking at the actual bug report, the issue manifests after suspend/resume with timeout messages and a switch to polling mode. This points to state not being properly reset during the resume sequence. The azx_resume function likely isn't reinitializing the codec communication state correctly.","signature":"EpYVCkYICxgCKkD2aCeCNkFATRVmGCKZNuiUt/CViv0db8DTLs6jzhyAULgSv1sl/odjGhEjSEOUDR0aQTUo798Li/Dzf3pPAb8QEgxNB+pIv9nzqfKgvVoaDGkKMUbB7eqU8sPYTCIwH2wxidjjHXgG/o46wRCy5dRxmX1JJxF93LkqaKyyJ14RbfkSH846+Ejo3OdxqFn2Kv0T3jaI4BSIFjtnNks0vUt2zV/c0lIO4ael0I68Fm6tuYE1x+phcvXcPmCwPpGdxjhDyAvW/HYE5M5BjUUfvWgCc0Aeb/Zxlu8eO86Ed0aNfJn6Fj41ZyjhIsCmJ5vGQrm7oVtW+vaneVqwau0OHVfNJTylleRHisIlFI6iOi1XHrrKhoG4VAxNwqUrfSgoiQ6jC73KDFhvjIUsxwDRjHESAnYOT/7yEGD25pdTnZ6s0nk6QECQexq59vyLK28EQBuSDagV9XNQTNi07GYMlCESZ4w3DfNPI3md0f38gTKN7s645RJy+QoOVfv6lUys/9nJBnYOKNNgIpUHRxCxWq3xHF7kNrgs48vpubdWf8ZmyqlsbccZdItVB5nG9OxdnFb/HJptitE40hOWra/AwxMCMOx/oinkTRjAxhpo776WCPUrT92ALeGN3mpA6P5ws6KpFqesWCVc4q1yJyhMdZLzB/vB9De/lueZFu3jfxpoVdJoYo18uvovHN3jS35HHQxC4fWcrp+1FLV1ODpoXdHHFzja5ESSH/JvkyQ1a+LzWMEB1pq+3l+4dGrKbxnsmpMc+NFEAiqhKX/TpdIZ3yuhqO/5hAcHN15zaqO8k33Djon1mttwqAf62Fk1atxFmcwdPWBsV5a4jTErmANf9SGEwlqyw0WclN6EQWE2/f3mM0i1vjXOmJ/U2oaG7l5uwVXdfSnqu2na+dDvdLH0aVaGJVitpDS7/bDkfAhPbVrvMXNirGbiNXHqzGksJFi4wDNJ1k63wseO8jFfctMwO2kheZ4Dz2aHdUFIf/Dpsga8jW7yx0gvg/1TSza30PvaJVX5VRPgmZntFY4W1DopBUZrBAAADJ5YAIUyX1epDEeLVefcm/AlhrkaqAH62O4Hdwp+WZtalzAWtgoKZOrRMzTrCBHVH0n5i4uIgnnnkML4z3zFgyr7CKxj5xcon85jNvNi6qH5AFfb1DP4AlZzE39qCUqrWLVqMOaD5If9gKrQVlUSmMKgRibS4DkHRqAD4QPxkXTyls16FWUiprklvk+BejEgneZ4ukD5OdItWMxnAW+BVHK9s5R3Quq603guIifGaCUtuMXTIBldRK2wIr579lO8PaSAeFKgfaQZM67o1NHNwc8trhSIk6B1g2A5JBWhVBrIkeP9HtDiOtXhmY9GJAt9/Hb71c0ewRqCNM0kSIGoWZ/iQxTgICXqIT6w5o40eL2cAzw0LikVj/t7hTgH5oDAmEKRIJ559Cfa5JEvbnDyKO5yBI/uZzedhHchLOtPETz+JGk5Rze+lp/MhOxzvyhwEU01rszwFFMMgmKDtCtBKsLFUtgz5nQ0NsYMRTy8inj8KpLAQdct8WzYiZObOpTLbNoIFd8Z8j1TmwLCK2HoNq7Yj7HVc41qcsdqFbz0NY6/55NC05RIktBviteHkOlFmXTFg0bca6ecSxgtxsbO+AF0t9zSEA3ylhJtNZTA4eQaggcgYp7UMaTIP9dT0iTp8CLPTxpnq6vHI5i/qbvLvIrUJbZhR+9yXjpfhlIlA0XDjqScE5+e2mJsuwbitXJrxwi9AGDXYHK8u2RuaaFtKgibxQ/zCXJPugYd8z+0fRZgFuzvQd6sHgauajQoNaDThdCfi2RAVKLq8ReQz/rgSQOKYXDSybHpmgkYSUdQRoK5hRLZheXd+Dl28x8uYaTmKR5ZIBdaWl4m+tvP7qmk6G0+YRKPHDVpyFpBI/YZ7jF5PEFKelXcE50rqpNDIn+krqtsZClvRwRxMW/ {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_014CTSpyhae8JAUtfAdkNViu","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"So `azx_stop_chip` does:\n1. Disables interrupts\n2. Clears interrupts\n3. Disables CORB/RIRB (releases command I/O)\n4. Disables position buffer\n5. Sets chip->initialized = 0\n\nIt should also reset polling_mode to 0 when stopping the chip, because polling_mode is a transient state that's only needed as a workaround when interrupt-based communication fails. What if the issue is in the initialization order or in the codec communication? Let me check if there's an issue with not resetting the polling_mode before acquiring the irq.\n\n\nThe error message \"No response from codec, disabling MSI: last cmd=0x00170503\" indicates that after the initial timeout triggers polling mode, subsequent failures lead to MSI being disabled and the IRQ being reacquired. However, the polling_mode flag remains set even after these recovery attempts, causing the driver to continue polling instead of using the newly acquired interrupt. This persistent polling_mode state prevents the driver from properly utilizing the restored interrupt mechanism after MSI is disabled and the IRQ is re-enabled.\n\nThe root cause appears to be that polling_mode isn't cleared when the chip stops and restarts. After suspend/resume cycles, when azx_stop_chip() disables the chip and sets chip->initialized to 0, the polling_mode flag remains set. During resume, azx_init_chip() reinitializes the hardware but does not reset polling_mode, causing the driver to stay in polling mode even though the hardware has been reset. This leads to codec communication failures manifesting as choppy sound with clicks separated by 2-second silences. The fix is to add 'chip->polling_mode = 0;' in azx_stop_chip() to reset the transient polling mode state when the chip is shut down, ensuring a clean state when the chip is reinitialized during resume.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":3,"cache_creation_input_tokens":141,"cache_read_input_tokens":50159,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":141},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"470d90dd-f926-49e7-ae0b-054b0a285722","uuid":"ea86f29f-90b8-4753-ac6b-adb208810379"}
